Median selection networks for a given number of inputs

The networks on this page can be used to find the median value of the inputs and are not full sorting networks.

The rows that yield the output(s) are marked in blue. For an even number of inputs, the average of the two outputs still needs to be computed by the application. Note that in this case, the two outputs are usually not ordered.
A median selection network with an even number of inputs can be converted into a "perfect halver" network by adding a single CE element connecting the two central outputs, however the networks on this page are not optimized for this.

Just like for the sorting networks list, the median selection networks have been defined in terms of two metrics:

  • Number of compare/exchange elements (CEs) - metric below called "size"
  • Number of parallel operation steps (layers), determining processing latency - metric below called "depth"

Provided is a minimum set of networks that each can be the best choice depending on how both criteria are weighted.

The additional "cost" metric is derived from the idea that each CE can be considered as a combination of a minimizer and a maximizer.
If both results are used, its cost is 2. If one of the outputs is discarded, one of the subcomponents can be removed and the cost is 1. The "cost" metric corresponds to the number of subcomponents as described in [Sekan04].

If no source is mentioned, the network was generated by the SorterHunter program, by applying postfix networks to the evolving network and removing them from the resulting sorting network.

In many cases, networks could also be derived from other median selection networks with a slightly different number of inputs:

  • Removing two inputs from a network for N+2 inputs.
  • For odd N, adding a central pair connecting the outputs of a network for N+1 inputs and then removing one input from the resulting network.
  • For odd N, starting from a network for N-1 inputs, add a 3-sorter to its two outputs and one new input.

For questions, remarks, or to contribute improved results please contact bert.o.dobbelaere[at]telenet[dot]be.
